<Author>NYCtraveler1500
<Content>Love this hotel! This hotel was a 100% pleasant surprise. From the mixed reviews, I was a bit nervous after booking -- could not have been more pleased with the place. When you first arrive - don't be surprised that it's in a street that seems more like an alley (it was my first time in Barcelona and apparently many of the streets are like this). The staff is exceptional -- every last person treats you as if you're in a 5-star, white-glove hotel. Stefano at the front desk is especially helpful and has great restaurant suggestions.The rooms are not strange in the least - they're incredibly practical and perfect for a business traveler who likes boutique style and doesn't take themselves too seriously (it's definitely not your grandma's hotel :) Good bed. Excellent size safe for laptops. Wireless and wired Internet. Marvelous shower and good towels. Terrific lighting in the bathroom and nice details, like a vanity area. The separate, private lounge across the hall is a small and comfortable space that is perfect if you need to work in your room - feels like you have a little ready-made office. The little cafe room downstairs that's open all day and fully included in your stay is a nice touch. Best moment ... I was late down for breakfast one day and they had just closed the breakfast room. Instead of turning me away, they said they could make me a continental breakfast ... I thought that in itself was very nice and hoped for a croissant and a cup of coffee. But they brought out so much food - one plate of breads, another of pastries, then cheeses, then meats, then sliced fruits ... just beautiful. That was the type of service I experienced from the moment I arrived until the moment I left.I wish I'd like the rest of Barcelona that much. Hopefully, Camper will open other hotels (maybe Paris or London?) so that I can stay more often ...

<Author>plusfour
<Content>Ultra stylish, and with substance... First time in Barcelona and I had high expectations - people had told me how much there was to do and how cool a city it was. I'd found a good looking hotel through my usual sources but the Casa Camper had been mentioned. From a peak around the hotel website it looked very funky and was only a bit more expensive than my other boutique-y option so I decided to go for it. And.......? I'm glad I did.First up, location.Casa Camper is on a tiny backstreet just off Las Ramblas - tourist centre of Barcelona - in an area called El Raval. Lots of guide books will tell you about how El Raval was the seedy hangout of Barcelona for years and, to be honest, I can believe it, but it now has the vibe of the place to be in Barcelona - lots going on, lots of shops, bars and people and right in the middle of it all. Location then, very good.Next up, the hotel itself.Very, very cool. The design, and maybe more to the point, the extent to which they've followed through the design is stunning - everything matches, everything looks bespoke and everything is very stylish, very modern and very, very cool. The lobby area has a fridge with cool design books and Camper shoes for sale, a massive map of Barcelona on the wall stylised to fit in with the rest of the hotel design and an iMac for you to check your email (oh, wifi is free too). The bedrooms have a 2-room setup (a big bedroom and bathroom - fabulous shower for sharing - and separate lounge across the corridor with hammock, TV and sofa) something which works very well. There are no mini-bars but there are 24 hour snacks and drinks (amazing selection!) available free in reception (alcohol is available, but not free) - all very welcome for a late afternoon topup - especially when Barcelona doesn't eat before 9:30pm! Breakfast is served in the same place and is a good continental spread.The bed was huge and comfy, the shower was massive and powerful (fab deluge head) and the Tivoli radio was excellent - although don't forget your iPod audio cable!Third, the service.Truly excellent. A thorough guide around the hotel and rooms on arrival and friendly, pleasant, cheerful staff ready to help at any point. Don't expect bell boys in morning suits and top hats, but do expect great service and a friendly attitude. Oh and they'll lend you the hotel bikes too...So then, the verdict....Casa Camper is a great boutique hotel - cool location, great design and excellent service. Not for anyone who likes The Ritz or the ultra-traditional 5* ideal, but if you want something that's stylish, funky, comfortable and well equipped, stay here. Not cheap, but highly recommended.

<Author>Mayfair Ranger
<Content>Part Luxury Hotel, Part Youth Hostel The Casa Camper enjoys a good location near the university, within a couple of hundred yards of the top end of La Rambla. Reception staff are very friendly and helpful, although many are foreign students and some therefore do not have an extensive knowledge of the city. The hotel claims to be eco-friendly (e.g. recycling bathroom water) so it seemed curious that the air-conditioning and lights were always left on after our room was made up each day.The suites are well thought-out with clean lines and decor, interesting features and strong colours. As some other reviewers have noted, the basic rooms have a curious arrangement whereby the living room is located across a public corridor from the bedroom. You might not feel comfortable crossing the corridor in your pyjamas or underwear - we were certainly glad to be in a suite.The hotel benefits from a great complimentary all-day help-yourself snack bar. A cooked breakfast is however also available to order.If you enjoy light, be sure to specify a preference for a high floor. The hotel is located on an alleyway and the lower floors are conspicuously dark.The Casa Camper is a 4-star hotel, yet with certain youth hostel characteristics. As such it is both unique and charming. Even as someone who would steer a million miles from a youth hostel, I can strongly recommend it.

<Author>Constance5
<Content>I'm fussy I'm fussy about where I stay. I like a comfortable bed, quiet, clean interesting space, kind staff, beverages in the AM. Hotel Camper fit the bill plus and one of the high lights of our trip to Barcelona. First a word on noise since this seemed to be a concern in some of the previous reviews. There was none. The hotel was an oasis of calm in an active, festive and throbbing city. The double glass doors to the lobby shut out all street noise. Jazz vocals played in the background. Our third floor bedroom was silent, the roof top sitting area was peaceful and as a bonus allowed a view of the nightly firworks. With the unfavorable exchange rate on the dollar and the exhorbitant price of even a light snack, having a more than adequatre, healthy 23 hour day and night buffet available was a cost saver and so convenient. Though the Barcelona food is a treat, there's too much to do in the city to be caught up in restaurant searches three times a day. Plus the food with it's emphasis on oil can be heavy. We enjoyed the hotel's fruit and salad. The bed was the right firmness and comfy, the room was dark, neat and elegant.My concern about the neighborhood was unwarranted. We were careful, the usual no swinging pocketbooks or back pant pocket valuables. Several blocks from Rambla on a well frequented street we felt safe night and even early morning going to our airport transport with luggage on tow. The location was perfect, a short walk to the action, but off the main drag. The staff was sweet and helpful, a little short on usual hotel concierge service. Worked out fine for us, we like to find our own way.Would love to come back and/or stay at another Camper boutique hotel elsewhere.

<Author>scotsguy61
<Content>Casa Camper, Casa by name: home by nature We had been in Barcelona for about a week in an apartment in the El Borne. We had a late flight home and had to be out our apartment by 11 am (the flight was at 9pm) and decided to move to the Casa Camper after seeing it on our way to MACBA.As other reviewers have pointed out (and in some cases seem to have missed the point of) the USP of Casa Camper is its unique room layouts, whereby everyone has what is essentially a suite, a bedroom and separate sitting area. The design takes advantage of this layout whereby the sitting area faces the (noisy) street, and is seperated by a corridor from the bedroom which is well insulated at the rear of the building. Compared to El Borne our night there was serene in its quietness.The functionality of the rooms has been criticised by some of the reviewers but to my mind the hotel bedrooms were well designed and equipped. The beds are huge, the sheets crisp the pillows soft. One of the best I've been in. The toiletries were top notch too. Aircon icy and two tvs one in each room.Staff were super friendly and gave us a late check out till 4 in the afternoon so our last day in Barcelona was releaxed and we had a chance to shower before we caught the plane home. All in all an oasis in the frenticism that is Barcelona.I highly recommend for couples, maybe not for families who may find it a bit sterile.

<Author>tangoLondon
<Content>Fantastic! Just returned from three nights at Casa Camper to celebrate our 25th wedding anniversary. Chose hotel from TripAdvisor site and was not disappointed. Would say this is one of the nicest hotels I have ever stayed in.The location is perfect - two minutes walk from Las Ramblas and also close to the 'old' part of the city which has some great restaurants. Hotel is down small side street off Las Ramblas and is totally peaceful. We had a suite ie. bedroom/bathroom/lounge area adjacent as opposed to other rooms which had lounge area across small corridor from bed/bathrooms. The suite was lovely - huge comfy bed; towelling bathrobes and slippers; large bathroom with best shower ever. Flat screen TV in bedroom and one in lounge area, which also had a lovely hammock!There is a breakfast area adjacent to reception. Food was excellent. As well as breakfast, there is food/drink provided on a self service basis all day for free - quality is excellent. Sandwiches/pastries/fruit juices/tea etc.Above all, the staff are wonderful. A complimentary glass of champagne on arrival (perhaps due to our anniversary?); an anniversary card in our room. Stefano at reception recommended a restaurant for us to try each night - no pressure, just gave us the addresses and directions. They were all great choices.One of the staff told us a Casa Camper was opening in Berlin next year - they should have them in every city!!

<Author>cheviot
<Content>funky hotel WE stayed for 3 nights at Casa Camper, Barcelona and mostly enjoyed it. THe best part was the position, once you and the taxi driver find it is very central to a great part of town. The down side for us was the liviing room/bedroom across the hall which had our 7 year old daughters bed, we did not feel comfortable leaving her across the hall. If you visit with small children make sure you book a room without the lounge across the hall.Apart from that the hotel is beautifully and simply decorated, a little dark in the rooms. The staff are helpful and the free food and drinks in the lobby a nice change from overpriced mini bars.

<Author>HubrisChicago
<Content>Charming, Convenient, and a Great "Service with a Smile" Staff We stayed on the third floor in a suite. The suites are at the end of the hallway on each floor (five total), and are the only rooms where the bedrooms and sitting areas are connected. The remaining rooms require you to walk across the hallway to your connected sitting area. Not a big deal (we peeked in an open room), but worth noting. I think the hotel only has about forty(40) rooms.The suites are clean, comfortable, and have great cooling systems. The beds are sufficient, the sheets are crisp, and the pillows are fluffy. The shower water pressure is great, and the bathrooms are roomy and well lit.The sitting area in each room will allow you to open french doors, and stand on a small balcony overlooking the street below. When you close the doors, you can barely hear any of the street noise below, and in the bedroom you couldn't hear a thing.The hotel also has a great rooftop deck, includes morning breakfast, and has a small cantina that is open 24hrs per day that allows all guests to grab a quick water, coke, juice, sandwiches, etc.. at their convenience ----- included in hotel cost.The staff was very attentive, helped us book tours, provided printed out maps to various restaurants  attractions, and in general were filled with super-positive energy. We were on a portion of our honeymoon, and the staff even sent up a little bottle of champagne with well-wishes. Nice.

<Author>Perthi
<Content>When in Barcelona, there is only one hotel: Casa Camper I am sorry about the people who had a bad experience at this hotel but this is the most interesting and one of the best hotels in Barcelona. First, it looks like an Art Gallery, secondly, the staff (specially Guillermo and the lady who cooks breakfast: she is a gem) are extremely friendly and helpful; thirdly, it is very central (just 2 minutes from Las Ramblas and Plaza Cataluna). Breakfast is excellent: you can have whatever you want. There is a good selection of snacks 24 hours tentempie including hot and cold drinks, cakes, soup, salads, etc., which you can take to your room or to the terrace. I used this service many times even at 3:00 am. The rooms are excellent. We stayed in a Suite with our private little balcony in a narrow street, a lounge, a bedroom with a Kingsize bed and a bathroom (The shower is a must). The whole place is like a small apartment. HOWEVER, there are 2 kinds of rooms: Suites and Rooms. The rooms are just like the Suites except that the lounge and balcony are separate so you have a corridor between your bedroom/bathroom and the lounge. We found that the Suites are very noisy SO I recommend not to book a Suite. Book a room. FINALLY, GUILLERMO (the Manager during the day) is wonderful: he is helpful, friendly, excellent, and he will do anything to sort out your problems. He is the heart of this hotel. Ask for him if you stay at this excellent hotel.

<Author>TravelerCool
<Content>Hot and noisy I booked this hotel based soley on trip advisor recommmendations; adn travelled there with my 2 boys for 4 days at the beginning of May. The taxi driver had no problem finding the hotel, even though I had taken the precaution of printing the map.On arrival, we were greeted by very pleasant reception staff and shown around the ground floor, which basically consisted of a seating area and a little room where you could have 24 hour complimentary tentempe. This consisted of breads, soft drinks, juices, water, crisps, doughnuts,crackers, nuts, cheeses, tomatoes. In a fridge there were simple salads,various sandwiches and desserts. All were clearly marked and looked fresh. The area appeared to be very claen. There were different bins for the different types of waste, which I thought was impressive.The only downside to this area was that, according to my 11 year old, it felt like being in an airport terminal. The lay out and the clinical athmosphere were not what we are used to. However, when in Barcelona.....I had booked a suite, simply because my 2 boys and I would not have fitted in a standard room. One of us would would have had to stay across the hall. The suite consisted of a bathroom, sliding door to bedroom, sliding door to living room with sofa bed and french windows to tiny balcony and street outside. Therefore, we had none of this hopping across the corridor to the living room that other people had. There was a television in both the bedroom and the living room. The bathroom was ok, though the tiling looked cheap and poorly finished.It is hard to pinpoint why, but, for us, it just did not work. It was as if I was back in the caravans of my youth! The dim lighting,the sliding doors, the sparse sense of the place, a vaguely musty damp smell.In any event, it was late so we unpacked and went to bed. I agreed to take first night on the sofe bed (Stupid mom eh!) Then the fun started. The room was very hot and though we tried to adjust the aircon, it remained very hot so we could not sleep properly. The living room was right beside the street so it was quite noisy until 2 or 3 am with people in the street; short respite, then noise again from 5am, presumably this time from garbage and cleaning trucks. I must have finally dozed at 8 or so because it was 11 before we finally woke, shattered, and ran down to grab something for breakfast before it finished. The selection was good, well presented and enjoyable.After breakfast, I went to reception and explained about the aircon problem. The girl was attentive and interested. She said that she would try to have it sorted for us. I explained thaif she could not get it fixed we were happy to move rooms. She told me that they were fully booked so I said that , if the problem could not be remedied,we would have to move to another hotel.We went back to the room( I think it was 35) to get sorted and within 5 minutes a gentleman appeared at the door. If memory serves, his name was Peter. He explained that there had been problems with the aircon and that he was happy to move us to another hotel. He would arrange to have our luggage transferred and we could go ahead, inspect the hotel, and confirm whether it was acceptable to us. This we duly did ( see report on hotel regina)We checked out shortly after and I have to admit that I was surprised to be charged the full rate; though the wine I had the night before was comped. I suppose i expected more of a gesture given that we had not slept and that much time was to be wasted changing hotel. In any event, I was too tired to say anything.I paid the bill and we just moved to the other hotel.All in all, the saving grace of this hotel was its staff. I found the service at all times to be excellent. However, it was not enough to overcome the clinical athmosphere,the broken air con and the noisy rooms. We won't be back.  
<Date>May 19, 2008

<Author>minimalbue
<Content>Excellent hotel for the young at heart I loved this hotel. The location just off Las Ramblas shopping street is excellent and the tiny street is a quiet relief from the crowds on Las Ramblas. I stayed in a suite that had a great floorplan and was roomy. The tiny balcony overlooking the street was sweet and the hotel roof deck was unused and romantic. My room was amazingly quiet. The staff was really friendly and helpful and their English was excellent.One big plus of the hotel is the canteen that serves free light food and non-alcoholic drinks 24/7. It was great to eat an early salad if one didn't want a heavy meal at 9PM. Alcohol was available for mini-bar prices. There is a shop that sells wine and booze a few doors down for reasonable prices, but closed during siesta.The interior design is clean- lined, modern and functional, but not high style. Certain older travellers who are accustomed to traditional hotels with traditional interior design and formality probably would find this hotel unsuitable. Be sure to bring a Google map with the hotel location with you to Barcelona to give to the taxi driver and let him/her know that taxis are allowed on the street in front of the hotel.One hint: finding the the front door to the hotel is a bit confusing. The door is a sliding glass panel located directly under the HOTEL sign that has a thick red stripe painted on it. Just stand there and the door will eventully slide open. Then walk through the black colored vestibule and the staff will open the interior door when they see you. Don't know the reason for the special security as the neighborhood seemed safe. However, the feeling of shelter inside was a nice plus from the busy crowded streets in Barcelona.

<Author>tziambra
<Content>"I felt like I was in a playhouse" I have been to Barcelona many times in the past few years and this time around, I decided to try Casa Camper. The hotel is by far one of the nicest ones in the city and probably the funkiest. I am sure there are other luxury hotel chains that will give you the feel of a normal hotel but Casa Camper is a different experience. Each room actually has two rooms across the hallway from each other. One is the bedroom and the other one is the hangout room. The colors are bright, there is a huge window for a wall in the back that overlooks in the Casa Camper courtyard. Most of the furniture is the room is trendy (you can also buy it at this famous design store in the city) and functional. The bathroom has an excellent shower and great products, shower gel, shampoo etc. The living room has a huge hammock in it, a couch and a flat screen tv. It is unconventional but if you really think about it, it is a great idea.  At the lobby of the hotel, there is a small restaurant area where you can get some food and snacks 24hours per day. This is included in the prices along with the breakfast. All the people working at Casa Camper were super-friendly and helpful. The location of the hotel is very central, just off Las Ramblas close the Plaza Catalunya and it is surprisingly quiet for how close to the action it is. The best thing about Casa Camper is that it feels like home. If, for example, you have been walking around the city for the whole day and you need sometime to relax, it is felt so much more fun to return to the hotel and hang out in the living room where you can take the food upstairs and chill and do not have to be stranded in a standard hotel room. I highly recommended to anybody who likes boutique, trendy hotels that diverge from the normal and expected.

<Author>Tim-Limbach
<Content>Top hotel in ideal location My wife comments, apart from the rooms in our suite being too dark, I don't know how I could fault it.I booked this hotel, following the many positive reviews I had read and wanted my wife to enjoy the no.1 hotel in Barcelona.On arrival we were invited to enjoy our choice from the extensive buffet, most salads, sandwiches and cakes being wrapped in individual plastic cartons. Guests are encouraged to recycle the waste.There is a fine selections of fizzy drinks (sodas) and fruit juices, as well as yoghurt and pastries, tea and coffee. All the snacks are described in Catalan and English. This buffet is available 24 hrs a day and is changed daily. Breakfast is also served in this buffet / lounge area and includes freshly squeezed orange / grapefruit juices, sliced fresh fruit, pastries, cold meats, cheeses, yoghurts plus food cooked to order by the charming chefs. I enjoyed pancakes with maple syrup.Our suite, consisted of a large bathroom, with tub and two types of powerful shower, fluffy towels and slippers / robes are provided. The bedroom had an enormous bed, plenty of shelf space, subdued lighting, a radio and flatscreen tv.The adjoining lounge had sofa, hammock, flatscreen tv and very narrow balcony.Each room had individually controlled a/c.There is a rooftop terrace available, with drinks for purchase, but it was too cold to enjoy.The situation is ideal, being minutes from Catalunya and Las Ramblas amd many other notable attractions.It is expensive at 270 Euros per night, but is worth a try.The staff are very helpful and friendly.

<Author>QueenA
<Content>I want to go back... Stayed 2 nights here with my partner. We had a room (or 2 rooms) on the 5th floor. the 2 room set up is fine - we never saw anyone else when we made the cross. The main room is nicely done but a bit dark when you're trying to find your money/room card/map etc. Got very attached to the hammock in the lounge that faces the tv while my partner had a siesta. All day buffet is fairly limited - sandwiches, salads, yoghurt mainly but good for a snack and who wants to hang out in the hotel lobby while you're in Barcelona?!Hotel is situated in the upper raval which is currently the hippest area of Barcelona. Contrary to what some people might have read, the upper raval is very safe, quite touristy but with bars/restaurants a plenty. Hotel is literally 3 mins walk from Museum of Modern Art. As an aside, the lower raval still has 'edge' so not a place to sightsee with the kids.Really recommend restaurant/bar Dos, Trice. 5 mins walk from hotel. Eat in the basement (smoking even if like us you don't smoke). Decor is a cross between a David Lynch film set and a brothel. ..Food really good and cheap. Full of locals. They do a good mojito too. this is the 2nd time I've been to barcelona and I can't wait to go back. Would stay at casa camper again too.

<Author>Coopers4
<Content>Different! This property suited our family very well. We are a family of 2 adults and 2 teenagers and having been travelling together for a month we all felt the need for some time apart. The unusual arrangement at Casa Camper, where each room has a separate living room across the hallway, provided exactly what we needed. The 'living room' has a tv, desk, couch and hammock, all of which were useful. The bedrooms are comfortable and quirky. There is no enclosed wardrobe, just open shelves and a line of Shaker style pegs the length of the bedroom on which to hang things - even the TV and hotel information hang from pegs. The bathroom is not enclosed and looks out on a wall stacked with aspidistra in pots. It is all stylishly executed and practical enough. The living rooms face the street while the bedrooms overlook a small courtyard so are very quiet.What really sold our 2 teenagers on the hotel though is the excellent lounge/breakfast/snack room on the ground floor. Not only is the buffet breakfast complimentary but drinks and snacks are available at no charge throughout the day. They loved being able to help themselves whenever they felt like it. The food was also very good.The staff here were very welcoming and friendly, with useful recommendations about where to go and where to eat. The hotel is small and has quite an intimate feel to it. It is also very well located , just off La Rambla in the Raval area. The Museum of Contemporary Art is just around the corner.

<Author>RonFinlay
<Content>Best hotel ever! Casa Camper is full of wit and fun, as well as having fantastic staff, being ecologically thoughtful and well-located. Bedrooms look out on to a 'vertical garden'; there's a hammock in each day room; shower water is recycled; the hotel has its own bicycles available for hire; and even the instructions on how to use the electric blinds are nicely self-deprecating! The all-day free snacks are a real boon, but most impressive of all are the staff, whom we found universally helpful and friendly. The hotel is within easy reach on foot of all the main sights, yet is nice and quiet. A top choice.

<Author>goonerbear
<Content>Casa Camper Superb Me and my wife stayed at the Casa Camper from Dec 18 2007 for 4 nights. From the moment we arrived the staff were excellent. In some 5* hotels we have stayed in the staff have been so pretentious its unbelievable (the Skt Petri in Copenhagen is a excellent example of this) however this is not the case here, they are all young and extremely helpfull and approachable, the fact they wear T-shirts reduces the stuffy atmosphere sometimes found in these sort of hotels.We had room 25 which is a suite,the bathroom,bedroom and lounge are all connected and not seperated by the corridor. this means you can use the balcony in the lounge without crossing the corridor, which is probably more important if you stay during the hot summer months. The room was superb and the bed extremely comfortable, never had a bad nights sleep.The hoel offers free food 24hrs a day, this includes pastrys, pasta, cakes, sandwiches, crisps, bottled juices, water and coffee, these areavailable in the lobby area,you just help yourself and take to your room or eat there as often as you like! A cooked breakfast is available, you just ask the friendly chefs and they cook it then and there along with a more continental style breakfast buffet.The hotel has a terrace which will be nice in the summer and a weird vertical garden.The location is superb just off Las Ramblas, just makesure the taxi driver knows where it is,ours didnt.All in all a superb hotel,excellent staff and great location.Recommended

<Author>Geoffram
<Content>Well, I'm sorry... but I'm obviously in the minority. How stupid to have a lounge on the other side of a public corridor to the bedroom. Why would I want to see others in their undies flitting to their loved ones across the corridor? But this is typical of the whole hotel: someone thought it a bright idea: like putting the bedrooms on the inside so that there was no window. Or the run of hooks across one wall so that the door to the bathroom couldn't close completely. Or for that matter having no minibar so that if you woke up in the middle of the night with a slaking thirst, you had to trot downstairs to reception to get a drink. Or what was pretentiously called tentempi茅 - hot and cold snacks throughout the day - which proved to be a pea soup in an electric tureen and some sandwiches inthe fridge. All in all, the hotel was designed for looks rather than practicality: fine if one was in one's twenties and paying 100 Euros a night, but this was more than twice that amount. Stick to making shoes, boys.

<Author>A_J_TLondon
<Content>Fantastic time at Casa Camper My husband and I have just returned from our first trip to Barcelona where we celebrated our anniversary at the wonderful Casa Camper. Nothing was too much trouble for the friendly staff and we simply had to write a review of the hotel as it really made our trip special. From the moment we arrived we were made to feel tremendously welcome and relaxed. We stayed in a suite on the 5th floor which was very spacious and hip. The bed was large and very comfy and the lighting set the perfect ambience. The room encompassed a large living area with plasma screen TV etc and a very relaxing hammock and french doors from which you could step out and look down on the street below. The bathroom was also nicely sized with generous products to use and a fantastic power shower (and bath) - just what was needed after a day sightseeing in barcelona. We loved the unique design of the hotel from the lobby area through to the gorgeous roof terrace from which we enjoyed many a drink in the early evenings before going out for late dinner. The other remarkable thing about Casa Camper is the free food served 24 hours a day in the cafeteria. You can literally help yourself anytime to a selection of sandwiches, salads, cakes, pastries, yoghurts, crisps and a wide range of juices and soft drinks. All of this is included in yoru room rate and was a welcome addition to our stay.The location is also brilliant - on a small side street off Las Ramblas. The museum of contemporary art is at the end of the street and there are numerous lovely restaurants/cafes/bars nearby such as 'Es' meditaerranean restaurant and 'El Lobo' tapas restaurant - both very enjoyable and off the main tourist strip of Las Ramblas. We had a fantastic trip and cant reccommend this hotel highly enough!

<Author>anon28
<Content>Fantastic stay- highly recommended We stayed here for two nights based on the Tripadvisor reviews and weren't disappointed. Take the airport bus from outside arrivals to the last stop Place Catalunya- only 5 mins from the hotel which is located down a little street about two blocks from the Ramblas (look for the little side street Bon Success just before La Poma restaurant on the left of the street). The hotel is very modern, stark but not soul-less either. We arrived early and a room was available although we had read it was better to get a room on the 5th floor so decided to wait for one of those. V. helpful staff (excellent english) kept our luggage for us and advised us on where to visit until later that afternoon. The room itself was quite big with dark red walls and black slate floors and faced onto a funky vertical garden of plants and the roof terrace. There is a tv and radio in the room, just across the corridor is your sitting room which is small but cute and overlooks the rooftops (from the fifth floor). The bed was really comfortable and the shower excellent. Just beyond the lobby is the eating area where food is available 24/7 (no additional charge as already included in your room rate). It's mainly healthy eating with a selection of salads, sandwiches, yoghurt and deserts. There is a breakfast chef who will make your eggs or pancakes to order. There is also free internet access and a library for guests. The hotel location is perfect- right in the centre of the city. If you are in BCN for a wend, there is very limited shopping on a Sunday but all of the tourist attractions are open. We took the bus tours and really enjoyed them. It was a great way to see the city- it gets cold on top of the bus so bring a jacket. We also visited La Roca Village (outlets)- big names were Zegna, Gant, Versace etc. There were no great bargains to be found though! We really enjoyed Casa Camper and would highly recommend it.

<Author>Sanibelle1
<Content>Quirky Casa Camper Perfect For Open Minded Travelers We stayed at the Casa Camper for 2 nights based on its outstanding reviews on Trip Advisor. This is not a hotel for everyone, but if you are open to new things and like contemporary, modern hotels, this just might be for you. It is located down a little street about two blocks from the Ramblas. Our taxi left us off about two blocks away despite our protests. We had just had a bag stolen at the airport and were not in the best frame of mind and ready to walk through the streets with our remaining bags. However, that was what we had to do as our taxi driver yelled after us, chastising us for even questioning the place where he let us out. The hotel is very stark and you have to be buzzed into the very plain lobby. The staff (all two of them) were young, hip and very helpful and they took us to our room to show us how things worked. The room was also very plain and somewhat cold, with dark red walls and black concrete floors. The main room faced a dark courtyard and the sitting area was actually across the hall which is somewhat inconvenient and we only used it to store our suitcases. It would prove very useful for a family with older children as I think it had a pullout couch. Amenities in the room were minimal but bottles of water were by our bed and Casa Camper's version of crocs were provided with new inner soles to wear in the room along with new age music coming out of the radio. The best part of the hotel was the open pantry in the lobby where breakfast was served. It was stocked 24 hours a day with nice salads, sandwiches, nuts, chips, yogurt, sodas, desserts, juices, etc and we took full advantage of it. They also provided internet access, including a printer, free of charge as well as shelves of books to take and share. The young staff could not have been more helpful and nice and the location was great.

<Author>Shady-Grove
<Content>Casa Camper is the Coolest! My family of 4 LOVED this hotel. We stayed in a suite so my husband and I could have the bedroom and the kids (ages 4 and 7) could stay in the living area. The living area came complete with flat screen TV, wall-size city map, and hammock! The location was perfect, just off La Rambla and Placa Catalunya on a cute narrow street near the Museum of Contemporary Art. The staff was exceedingly helpful, the decor cool and modern, and the rooms were far bigger than we expected. The large bathroom even had the option of a rainfall-type shower head. No minibar charges here--there was free food about 23 hours a day. In the morning they would make you pancakes or eggs along with bread selections, yogurt, drinks, etc. The rest of the day you could choose from a variety of sandwiches, cheese, yogurt, soup, juices, bottled water, and soda. Totally appreciated when you are jet-lagged and your eating is off-schedule. They also have a roof deck, bicycle rental, book exchange, wine for sale, and enjoyable bath products. We handled our reservation via email with no problems. We can't wait to return to Barcelona and Casa Camper!

<Author>mdp_az
<Content>Can't get much better than this! This is without a doubt the best hotel I've ever stayed in. The staff were top notch and provided a lot of personal service, great recommendations and a relaxed and friendly vibe. The property itself is awesome in a nice location near the Rambla, but far enough removed so that once inside your sleeping room you hear nothing but silence (unless you've returned after turn down when you'll hear the Tivoli radio playing soft classical music). The rooms are funky, minimalist, and quite comfy. The bed was awesome, there was adequate storage for clothes and extra luggage on the shelves, and the save was very convenient. The bathroom was amazing...words cannot do that shower justice. It did my enviro mind well knowing that water was solar heated and being re-used, b/c I definitely lingered in that shower for longer than normal! The vertical garden was a nice and unique touch, and the shade was great for creating a completely dark room. Across the hall, the lounge was so nice to come back to after a long day in the city. We'd pick up some drinks and snacks in the Tentempie (no addl. cost, of course!) and relax on the sofa while watching the nice sized LCD TV. I also opened the terrace doors a couple of times and chilled out in the hammock. Breakfasts were awesome...pancakes were amazing and like nothing I can make at home. The rooftop terrace was very nice and provided a beautiful view of the city and Tibidabo, and on the crowds below heading to/from the Rambla. So, now for the negatives. The lighting in the room and lounge was not very good, but was adequate in the bathroom. Some of the light switches seemed not to operate anything or function correctly. The TV in the room had different (and less) channels available than the one in the lounge. Minor complaint I know, but it just seemed a bit strange. There were more English channels available in the lounge, which is where I watched the most TV...go figure. The wooden bikes looked very cool, and we were hoping to take a couple out for an hour or so for a ride to the beach. I never saw anywhere that there was an additional cost for the bikes before booking, however they quoted a rental rate of something like 15 euro for a 1/2 day per bike. While that is not painfully expensive, I think they could do a better job of advertising the bikes as an amenity that costs extra. The only other negative is that I'm not still there.

<Author>Sirbo
<Content>Funky, Finesse, Fabulous Stayed at this funky little hotel in September 2007. Casa Camper has very own unique character and from this extends a cool culture that is unforgettable. The Hotel is fantastically located just off the main Ramblas in a small street - somehow Taxis manage to get you right to the door and that's where the staff come into their own. I have stayed at hundreds of hotels over the years both for business and pleasure, but I have yet to find a more personal, attentive and professional team than those at Casa Camper. These guys seem to enjoy every moment of their work and they treat every customer as an individual. The hotel is quirky both in its rooms and in its set up. I managed to book a suite which was excellent with a good sized bathroom, a large bedroom and a leisure area/come lounge with a LCD TV and Hammock etc. I checked out the normal rooms too and they were just as cool. The difference between the two being that you have a lounge room across the corridor from your bedroom in the standard rooms.Casa Campers quirkiness extends to snacks 24/7 and for me the coolest branding feature which were the Camper styled bicycles. We rented these wooden (yes wooden) bikes and cycled the whole length of the promenade along the beach. Too say it made people stare was an understatement, but what a way to get around Barcelona.In some respect these bicycles summed up the whole Casa Camper experience for me. Reliable, eye-catching, unforgettable, quirky, quality and fun in a city that is lovely. I heard we can expect a Casa Camper in Berlin next. Book me in now please.James - Winchester (UK)

<Author>2IrishYoungOnes
<Content>Casa Camper, oh so good! My husband and I stayed for five nights at Casa Camper in Barcelona and truly it was one of the best holidays we have ever had. I had been trying to decide whether to book with Casa Camper or another hotel. I was going to surprise my husband on the accommodation front so I was a little nervous as I wanted to get it right. Casa Camper as it is not your traditional type of hotel and I worried that perhaps it would be too funky for us. Don't get me wrong we are mid-40's, young at heart but I for one like my comfort especially as I travel a lot for work and I was worried my husband might not be too crazy on this hip design concept. I was going out on a limb here or so I thought. He wasn't disappointed and neither was I. Comfort and hip were parallel, nothing was sacrificed.The design of this hotel is superb. It's the finer details that are looked after. From the massive beds with pure cotton bed linen, air conditioning, bottles of water being left in your room, a large safe for all your valuables, your bed being turned down with classical music tuned on your radio lulling you into your bedroom to huge fluffy bath towels; robes and slippers at your disposal. The showers are incredible, like a fire hose which definitely wakes you up. We had a suite so also had a bath and that was a luxury to soak in after a long day pounding the streets of Barcelona sightseeing. The hammock placed right next to the windows (with French doors and a teeny, tiny balcony 鈥?just perfect), so you can absorb the Catalan vibe from the streets below. The music that plays in the reception area and lifts is all designed, not just your regular CD's on a loop. I can't say that I heard the same songs twice and the music at breakfast was always nice and jazzy. It was great! The help yourself to salads, snacks and drinks anytime was brilliant. You would think that you would over indulge but you didn't. Water was a lifesaver. Just bring up a couple of bottles to your room and then more was delivered later. The breakfasts were great. The chef cooked what you ordered in the line of eggs, tortillas, bacon, etc. There were cold meats, cheeses, lots of perfectly presented sliced fruit (no pith!), pastries, yoghurt, cereals, bread to toast, juices, tea, coffee, I can go on...The city is a walker's city so the location of the hotel is spot on. About two blocks off Las Ramblas but very, very quiet. You might hear the green parakeets chatting away in the daytime on the palm trees nearby - amazing to see so many of them. The roof terrace is a great place to chill, grab a drink and take it up there. A real feel of the city, with views as far as the eye can see. Boy, this place was the best; totally different, great atmosphere and absolutely fantastic staff (who were friendly and most helpful but not intrusive). Because it was so relaxed and chilled, the staff really made it for us. There was always a friendly face, a Hello! and How was your day?. It was never any trouble to recommend somewhere, book a restaurant or post a letter. They were so kind. And their recommendations were spot on. It was also nice that they asked us about a tapas bar we had been raving about because one of the other guests wanted to go there. That was cool to share info. Very observant!I had read up on Trip Advisor prior to booking this hotel and as one reviewer had said he would go back in a heartbeat - I can understand that. We plan to go back next year. The hotel might be a little more expensive than others but it makes sense to us to stay somewhere where we know it will be comfortable, clean, safe and friendly. Hats off to Casa Camper! Excellent - Five Star Rating all the way!Well done! To all the staff who were just great, thank you and especially Fernanda, Gemma, Guillermo and Sarah A seriously funky but extremely welcoming and comfortable hotel. Apparently, they will be opening one in Berlin sometime soon - I always wanted to visit that city too!

<Author>Karenherts
<Content>Different! My husband and I stayed at Casa Camper last weekend and had a great stay. When you arrive at the hotel, there's an immediate wow factor and the fact that you can only get into the reception area with a special swipe card made us feel quite priveleged!The rooms were great, but to be honest I'm not sure that the two rooms (one being a bedroom and one being a lounge across the corridor) really worked for me. But it was a nice novelty and I can imagine would be great if you were travelling in a family or with a few other people.The bedrooms were a good size though and the fittings were top quality. I really appreciated the little design touches like the wall of plants outside the window (hard to explain, but very cool), the light fittings etc. I ended up taking lots of pictures as inspiration for our own home!The bottles of wine and beer in reception were a good idea and we'd come back to the hotel after eating out and buy a bottle of wine to drink on the sixth floor veranda. If it was closed for the evening the staff were really helpful and opened it up (although you need to get out at the fith floor and walk up one flight of stairs). It was like our little haven above the hustle and bustle of the streets below.The 'open' self service area was also a really nice touch for the odd snack and soft drink and breakfasts were really tasty.All in all we really enjoyed our stay. It wasn't the best hotel we have ever stayed in, but it was the quirkiest and I felt a real sense of personality, that I haven't experienced in any other hotel. All in all we would definitely recommend.

<Content>Offering something genuinely different (and brilliant!) Offering something genuinely different (and brilliant!). We鈥檝e been fortunate enough to stay at some very luxurious hotels over the recent years. There are far more luxurious hotels than Casa Camper. It doesn鈥檛 have a restaurant, concierge service, 24hr room service or a fitness centre. What it does have is unique character offering a unique experience without being your usual contemporary, but superficial, minimalist setup. Location - It鈥檚 perfectly placed in one of the most charismatic districts and is opposite a very cute infant school with glorious palm tree garden frontage. We have a 14 month old daughter and we took her to the small swing park in the square just around the corner surrounded by cafes. There are great caf茅鈥檚 and restaurants (Mama Caf茅 and Es) seconds from the hotel. You can also walk to the gothic quarter in 5 mins.Service 鈥?I鈥檝e never had service like this before. You need lots of it with a baby and they gave in abundance. Friendly, informal, pre-emptive 鈥?fantastic. Felt different from the Four Seasons style 鈥渨e鈥檒l give great service because you鈥檙e paying for it鈥? They spoilt my daughter to death, organised food to be brought in for us (including carrying it from a local restaurant), provided us with really helpful tourist advice etc etc. BRILLIANT!Style 鈥?The architect really did an amazing job on this place. With a standard room you get two rooms. A lounge and a bedroom with bathroom. The lounge is on the street side and the bedroom faces the vertical garden. In the bedroom, silence. In the lounge with the balcony overlooking the narrow pedestrian street, atmosphere. You feel connected to the city. We were on the first floor and it did get quite loud with people talking, skateboarders and the odd mo-ped. We actually loved this because you could feel the personality of Barcelona. With a young child having somewhere to sit and have a glass of wine, whilst being completely separate from the baby was a true godsend. The rest of the hotel works so well with stylish and surprisingly practical design. The music, 24hour caf茅, roof terrace, room design, eco friendly nature (even the water is recycled!) furniture etc all work together perfectly.Value 鈥?for what you get this is amazing. It鈥檚 affordable and the service/environment makes you feel great. Book now, consider no other.We did leave wearing two pairs of new Campers purchased from the shop around the corner. I suspect many other do the same. Ingenious, really.

Prior to our stay at Casa Camper, I emailed the hotel requesting a bottle of champagne and a fruit basket to be placed in our room for our wedding anniversary. We took the Aerobus which took us to Placa Cataluna within 20mins and a very short walk (about 5mins) we arrived the hotel. It is very secure and you need a pass to get through the door. When we arrived the receptionist was busy checking in another guest and a member of staff took us and showed us around the snack bar and got us settled with a drink whilst we waited for the receptionist to finish. the hotel have lots of tourist information - maps, guides, general info. The hotel room was very comfortable and everything was provided for you - even condoms!! Our Champagne and fruit was laid out very romatically in our lounge room and this room was aldso very comfortable. I know that you do not go on holiday to watch TV but after a long day of travelling, all we wanted todo was have a shower and relax with a glass of bubbly and film and it was nice that we had the option to watch a film in english!!. Breakfast was good and the staff were very helpful. After we checkeed out of the room, they allowed us to remain in the lobby/dining area to have a drink before we set off. We would not hesitate staying here again and we are looking forward to seeing more of these hotels appearing around the world - apparantly there are plans for belgium next.

<Content>What a place to stay... I stayed in Casa Camper summer 2006 with my family. This boutique hotel is a fantasitc place to stay. I highly recommend it to anybody considering staying in Barcelona. Firstly, the location is ideal- just off Las Ramblas, therefore there is no noise to be heard, ensuring a great stay. The shower itself alone is fantastic (v.powerful).Each room has its own 'lounge' opposite, with a sitting area, hammock and another flat screen tv- somewhere to relax after a long day. This area has a view of a side street, just off Las Ramblas. The sevice in this chic hotel is brilliant, as are the staff who work here. Conclusively, I recommend this hotel, as there were no faults to be found. Although, some prefer a bar area, and this hotel does not provide one- but who needs this when you are in the busy city of Barcelona? I would definitely return- it's probably the most luxurious hotel that i've ever stayed in.

<Author>quantum_jane
<Content>A reality check -- cool hotel, but disappointing service all around My husband and I are writing this review together from our Casa Camper hotel room! We are here on our third night, and we have been saying for the past 72 hours 鈥渁dd that to the Trip Advisor review!鈥?So we thought we鈥檇 write it down now, since the list has grown so long and while it is still in our memory. We call this review The Reality Check 鈥?since we booked the hotel based on the glowing 鈥渂est hotel ever鈥?reviews, and in reality, we have had one problem after another with this hotel. We have mixed feelings after our stay, and wanted to share them. We splurged on this hotel, and the level of service was just not up to what we would expect. (Hotels we enjoy a lot, by comparison, include the Langham Plaza in Hong Kong, the Four Seasons in Sydney, and the Avenue Hotel in Copenhagen 鈥?to give you a sense of where we鈥檙e coming from.) We give in two stars for service, five stars for location and design -- we average it out to 3.5/4 stars.First, the positive: This hotel is in an unbeatable location. That alone is a great reason to stay here. Also, it has a very cool, hip vibe, great showers, and the rooms are smart and well-designed. However, we have had a string of problems throughout our stay that frustrated us greatly, especially at the rate we paid 鈥?220 Euro or 330 US dollars per night. We wanted to share them so that those of you who book here can temper your expectations a bit. We recommend that travelers looking for excellent service and concierges to think about booking elsewhere. - SMOKY ROOMS. The first night we checked in, we were given a room that smelled very strongly of cigarette smoke, even though it is a non-smoking hotel. We called down to ask about this, and the front desk acknowledged that they had smelled the smoke earlier when the made up the room. They said that they had opened the window in the bathroom and hoped that had helped, but it hadn鈥檛. There was no other room to move us, they said, and they had no way to clear the smoke out. So we spent our first night sleeping in a room that was very uncomfortable for us, as non-smokers. This is a big deal for me, as I hate sleeping in smoky rooms. It really made for an unpleasant first night, and we were frustrated that they had noticed the problem earlier and not taken sufficient steps to resolve it before we checked in. To spend $330 USD for a cigarette-reeking room just made me sad. - THEY FORGOT TO GIVE US OUR WAKE-UP CALL. There is no alarm clock in the room. You need to rely on the wake up call or travel with your own 鈥?which we didn鈥檛. So the second night, we were recovering from jet lag and requested a wake up call an hour before our dinner reservation at Comerc 24. They forgot to call us. We woke up ourselves eventually but it was a rush and we had to call the restaurant and request a later seating. With no alarms in the rooms, if you can't trust the front desk to give you your wake up call -- well, that's just not cool.- MANY FRONT DESK ERRORS. We depended on the front desk a couple of times, and we were really let down. First, when we really needed a cab quickly, they were unable to get one for us, even though when we checked in, we asked how difficult it was to get cabs and they said that it was no problem, to just call down. When they failed to get us a cab, my husband ran out into the street in front of the hotel and chased down a cab that had been parked out in front of the hotel. It seemed like something we could have gotten some help with 鈥?again, this is just a level of service. Later, we requested help booking train tickets. They said they would take care of it. But after a few hours we found out we had to go to the train service ourselves because you are unable to book those particular tickets over the phone. We only found this out because we stopped by the desk to inquire if everything was set. If we hadn鈥檛 asked, we would have returned home late at night, unable to get to the station and without any tickets for the next day. Also, the hotel says there are bikes to borrow, but when we checked on Saturday morning, they didn鈥檛 have any. Alas. These are little things, but my god, they add up!- FLAMENCO DANCING ON THE ROOF. If you want to sleep at midnight on a Saturday night, you might be in trouble 鈥?there was a troupe of Flamenco dancers on the roof two floors above us, which made for unbelievable stomping noises for a very long time. Although we were greatly disturbed by the noise, we weren鈥檛 allowed to even go up to the roof to enjoy the show, since it was for a private event. That also meant the Terrace, which we were hoping to hang out at Saturday night, was closed to us, which was disappointing. By itself, this wouldn鈥檛 be a big deal, but honestly, after all the other grief, it was just too much.CONCLUSION: We would only book here again only if we could do so at a reduced rate. If you are an extremely relaxed traveler, and the problems we had wouldn't be an issue for you, then by all means, this is a cool and comfortable hotel in a great location. If you want to be able to depend on the hotel for help with things or if you really need to get a good night's sleep, there might be better places for you in Barcelona.

<Author>hotelguruoslo
<Content>Hip, Relaxed, Convenient, Original I am a hotel snob - I admit it. I travel too much not to be. I always look for something unique but of high quality. Casa Camper fits the bill perfectly. I loved this place from the moment I entered.Staff are friendly and unpretentious. Location is convenient and real (as in not being the 100% tourist hell that Barcelona seems destined to become). The snacks and drinks available 24-7 make life easy. The rooms are comfortable, stylish and practical. Tivoli radios, sandals and condoms are left out for you to use. I stayed in a 'suite' located at the end of the hallways where the living area, bedroom and bath are all combined. I realize now that there is no advantage to this set-up over the normal 2-room arrangement for less cost. In fact, the bathroom and shower in the suites are not as nice! I would recommend not getting a 2nd floor room. The baseline from the lobby music comes through loud and clear. For sunshine and decreased street noise on the living room side of the building, get a room on the 4th floor or higher. All the bedrooms are quiet due to their location on the inside of the building. Although I love Hotel 1898 for the luxury and rooftop pool, I will not stay anywhere else but Casa Camper when in Barcelona now.

<Author>rsp1
<Content>Excellent stay at unique hotel. Casa Camper is a very unique hotel in the El Raval section of Barcelona, relatively close to the top of the Ramblas. The location is great -- Raval is roughly equivalent to the Lower East Side / E Village of New York (many students, hip scene, etc.). The hotel is close enough to the Ramblas to make anywhere in the city an easy walk (Gothic/Born, Pl Catalonya, etc).The hotel itself is interesting. The rooms are really composed of two separate rooms (divided by the hallway). The main room has the bedroom and bathroom. The second room is a lounge with hammock and desk and large framed wall-map of the area.The bedroom has a flatscreen, safe, Tivoli radio (with aux input for ipod). Storage space is plentiful and there are some creative touches in the bathroom area. The lounge has another flatscreen and telephone. The whole hotel has free wifi. Surprisingly, there was turndown service in the evening. The best touch, however, is the free food/drink available 24/7 in the lobby (soda/bottled water - even redbull, snacks, coffee, sandwiches/salads, etc).The staff is incredibly helpful and generally speaks excellent English.

<Author>sgbslo
<Content>A unique hotel We stayed at the Casa Camper for 2 nights after a cruise. Before our cruise we stayed at the Hotel Claris which is totally different from the Casa Camper but we liked both hotels.The Casa Camper is an eco-friendly, young, hip place. The staff are all young and wear t-shirts with the hotel logo. They were all very helpful and knowledgeable about the area. The rooms are somewhat minimually furnished but very comfortable. The bathroom is nicely equipped and the shower is huge and has a rainfall nozzle. In addition to your sleeping room you also have a little sitting room across the hall with a sofa, desk, hammock and a small balcony. The only thing I didn't like about the bedroom is that the only window is in the bath area and it looks out on an enclosed courtyard so there's not much natural light in the room. The rate includes breakfast and snacks 24 hours. The snack selections were surprisingly good and included sandwiches, salads, fruits, cookies etc.The location is on a street in El Raval near the contemporary art museum and very near La Ramblas. It had a nice neighborhood sort of feeling yet was very convenient.

<Author>LLSL
<Content>Love the shoes, love the hotel... We were interested to see how Camper shoe design would translate intoa hotel. And like the shoes, this place is comfortable, user-friendlyand quirky. As standard you get two rooms, one is a mini-lounge across the public hotel corridor from the bedroom. This was fine except that is where the extra bed is, and we couldn't leave our 8yr old son in what is effectively a separate hotel room. There is a mechanism for opening the doors without a key but he was too short toreach one switch. Never mind, he slept with me and my husband got the extra bed! Except there is no toilet there, so he had to come in and out in the middle of the night. This aside, everything else was great. They have thought of the smallest detail including a nightlight in the toilet, a fantastic shower, automatic blinds which really cut out the light, and a whole wall of hooks to hang your stuff on. there is no mini-bar-but instead you get a free all day snack buffet, which was wonderful. Breakfast was delicious,and the chef will cook up any of your favourite breakfast dishes. The receptions staff are tremendously helpful with directions, bus numbers etc. Overall a great experience. (By the way there is a Camper shoe shop just metres away from the main entrance...)

<Author>Natmandu
<Content>A great place. I stayed at Casa Camper partly on the strength of the reviews on this site, and have to agree with everyone that said what a great place it is. This was my first time in Barcelona, and Casa Camper made it all the better. Close to La Rambla, and sat in the heart of the funky, arty, resurgent El Raval, the location is superb. The Mercado de la Boqueria is nearby, as well as several really good value cafes and restaurants. The Metro at Plaza de Catalunya is ten minutes walk, giving access to everything in Barcelona.Casa Camper itself is a breath of fresh air for someone who has stayed in hotels from budget dives to swisher places, and never been entirely satisfied by any of them while enjoying elements of all of them. It's modern, with minimalist, utilitarian features and shaker styling, and yet feels very comfortable indeed - imagine an almost 'hostel'-like atmosphere, but with the feeling of comfort of a more expensive hotel. The standard rooms give a separate bedroom and mini lounge, with the bedroom thoughtfully placed away from the street - these rooms come complete with flat screen TV, plenty of room, and a hammock in the lounge for a siesta. The shower was the best I have ever used.The emphasis on sustainability is in evidence everywhere - the water from the showers is all recycled and used again to flush the toilets, all of the glass, plastic and card is recycled, and most of the hotel seems to be made from recycled materials - very much in keeping with the Camper philosophy. This isn't however all crochet and joss sticks - this is a slick, modern design hotel.The food in the 24 hour canteen is free, the breakfast is free, everything is well thought out, and the staff are brilliant. I could have stayed just another night, and another...Easily my favourite hotel anywhere.  
<Date>Feb 28, 2007

This time I could not book a suite and stayed and one of the rooms, and enjoyed having a separate private lounge to chill out and rest. It felt like home. <Author>coreyman97
<Content>cool hotel but beware of security!!! my family stayed here for 6 nites over christmas/new years. i booked it due to the reviews and it is a very cool place as most people have stated. so why the mediocre review? as my family and i were checking in we were told to leave all of our luggage at the front desk and to take a quick tour of the main floor. we were assured it was safe. the tour took all of a few minutes and when i returned, my knapsack was not there with all of my electronics and personal items. the check in manager said it was impossible and it never happened there. she also went on to question if i even had the bag since she had not seen it - though i had just given her my passports from the bag. i was told they would check the surveillance video and let me know if thay found anything. well of course the video showed someone lurking and stealing my bag when the front desk people turned their backs.i was told to go to the police station and make a report and they would see what they could do to compensate me with insurance. there is a fair amount of this petty thievery in barcelona so i was advised to come back real early the next day when i could take care of it in 1 hour rather that 3 or 4 as there were many similar cases. after making the report i was advised by casa camper that they were not insured unless i was mugged or physically had the bag ripped away from me. even though i was told by the hotel staff to leave everything and it would be safe, they couldn't do anything. they did say that i would receive a 15% discount on my stay - 2 rooms for 6 nites. while i appreciate the gesture it amounted to about 25% of what i had lost. i have emailed the owner of camper on 3 occasions to see if an organization as professional as theirs would do the right thing but i have not rec'd a reply. so just beware - the hotel is cool and our stay was enjoyable. but keep your bags and items close to you and when you are told to leave your belongings and they will be safe - DON'T DO IT!!!

<Author>Kradjian
<Content>Pedestrian Chic Stayed with my wife over New Years and concur with most of the reviews. The staff was excellent, especially Guillermo. The food lounge saved us an exceptional amount of money, allowing us to splurge on dinners. Location was central although if you have a lot of luggage take a cab as it sits on a tiny side street and typically very crowded. Very tight quarters but that is Europe. Don't expect elegance here, this is stricty an art nevaux atmosphere complete with somewhat tricky fixtures. Don't forget your electric converters! The shower was great and allowed us to replenish our resources after all the wonderful walking. The lounge room is seperated by a common hallway, however, served its purpose well when one spouse wanted to sleep and the other didn't. The sleeping arrangements kept it from getting a perfect score - the bed was small, a little uncomfortable and low to the ground. And the hallway is extremely noisy so if you are a picky sleeper may want to keep in mind. However, as an overall value this hotel is extremely hard to beat and we would consider returning.

<Author>USAconcierge
<Content>Fantastic--One Of The World's Great Boutique Hotels This is a hotel that has its act together. I chose this hotel because I'm the concierge at the No. #4 rated hotel in the United States on Tripadvisor, the Holiday Inn Historic District in Charleston, South Carolina, and whenever I travel I always like to stay at hotels that are highly rated on Tripadvisor so that I can learn tips and techniques to help me do even better at my own job. In my job as a concierge, I try to dazzle my guests every day with great customer service, but as result it's very hard to impress me when I stay at other hotels. Well, I'm here to say right now that I was completely DAZZLED by the level of customer service at Casa Camper. If you want to learn all the qualities that make up a great hotel, you need to stay at Casa Camper. Before my arrival, I asked the staff to recommend a tour guide to take us around Barcelona. They recommended someone and I tried several times to contact her by e-mail to no avail. So I e-mailed Casa Camper--could you try to track her down for me? Within two hours, I had an e-mail from the tour guide I was trying to reach, who said that Casa Camper had contacted her about my efforts to reach her and profuse apologies about her slowness in getting back to me. Now THATS customer service! When Casa Camper heard I was having trouble reaching this tour guide, they made my problem THEIR problem! We were taking trains all over Spain, but one of the tickets we were told could only be bought locally, not over the phone. So I e-mailed Casa Camper--could they get them for me? Within two hours, I received an e-mail from Casa Camper saying that they had already bought the tickets for me and would be waiting for me when I arrived! Wow---these people were really starting to dazzle me! When we finally arrived in early November, I immedietely fell in love with the decor of the hotel. There was a stunning mural of Barcelona on the wall and the whole place exuded an air of class and cool. When we checked in, something happened which I've never seen at a hotel before. One staff member took our passports and credit card while another one took us around and gave us an introductory walk around the hotel to explain the concept of the hotel and how it worked. This lasted at least 10 minutes and I later observed them doing this walk with other guests. They said they tried to do this with ALL the guests--it really made you feel special. I LOVED this idea. I LOVED the breakfasts---they made me a great ham and eggs or omelette every morning just the way I liked it and couldn't have been nicer about it. The rooms were ultra-chic and cool. The showers were the best I've ever encountered---fantastic water pressure that would come down like a waterfall. Everything was very, very clean. The beds were great, with huge pillows to rest your head against. When you got your wake-up call, they did something I've never seen at a hotel---they would ask you if you wanted them to call you back in 15 minutes just in case you went back to sleep!!! How innovative. When have you ever had a hotel ask you THAT before? The other innovative thing is this concept of the the 24-hour cafe in hotel where you could get snack or a drink at any hour of the day without having to pay anything. I loved this idea, too--although I will say it tended to be really healthy snacks. I suggested that they consider putting out some chocolate-chip cookies, oatmeal cookies, perhaps even some carrot cake for the junk-food junkies staying in the hotel. If they did that, then they 24-hour cafe concept would have been REALLY amazing! The best thing about this hotel, though, like all great hotels, is the staff. You can have the greatest rooms in the world, but without great staff, the hotel has no soul. The staff here speaks English fluently (a big plus in Barcelona, where a surprisingly large portion of the people have little grasp of English) and is in general, top-notch. I got a chance to speak with the General Manager, Nathalie Porta. She came up to me and and asked how my stay was going. Like most of the staff at Casa Camper, she was absolutely stunning to look at. I asked her, What is your secret? How do get such great staff? She said, We teach the staff one thing--never assume anything. Great advice. I sat down with her and told her my impressions and what she could do to make it an even better hotel. To my amazement, she took notes! This is the mark of someone who was born for the hotel business. She didn't think she knew it all--she wanted to know what she could do to be even better! Other stand-outs among the staff---Gemma was a super-star. She also was an example of someone who was born for the hotel business. She gave the feeling she really cared about my stay and bent over backwards for us! Maude was a total sweetheart. She did the introductory walks of the hotel and was, in general, fabulous. Cristina did the e-mails beforehand and was just as nice in person as she was by e-mail. Marilo at the front desk was also super-nice. I have only one criticism--the tour guide that they recommended for us to take us on private tours around Barcelona was good, but not great. I suggested to Nathalie that they set up a program with the staff where once a month they pay each one of the staff to go out and take some interesting new walking tour or visit some new exhibit at one of Barcelona's many museums so that they can always have current and up-to-date suggestions of things to do for the guests. If they did this, they might have found a better tour guide to recommend to me. But if you don't pay the staff to do this, they get busy and never get around to it. As a concierge, I know I am as only as good as my suggestions.  The bottom line--an innovative, ultra-chic hotel, in a great location, with super-friendly staff willing to bend over backwards for you ((and great breakfasts too!) I loved it and would never consider staying at any other hotel if I ever return to Barcelona. I liked it that much!Kevin McQuadeChief ConciergeHoliday Inn Historic DistrictCharleston, South CarolinaUSA

<Author>aristoph
<Content>Twin room concept just doesn't work Ok, first the great things about Casa Camper. It is very well located, just off la Rambla but in a relatively quiet side street. The staff are all young, very friendly and speak great English. While I was sceptical about the self-service food and drink concept at first it actually works very well in a hotel of this size (just 25 rooms) and there is a wide choice of snacks and drinks available. The main bedroom in your set of two rooms is large and well designed, with a beautiful walk-in shower (however using it does fill your whole bedroom with steam and humidity as there is no separating door). The fittings are all new and of high quality. All this is very very good.So why just a three-star rating then? The problem is that the split living-room/bedroom design with a corridor separating the two spaces just doesn't work. While we never actually used our living space that's not really a big issue as the bedroom is more than big enough to live in comfortably for two nights. No, our complaint was the noise every time our neighbours crossed the corridor between their two rooms. The doors are spring-loaded and slam loudly, made much louder by the hard floors in the corridor and rooms. Worse, there is a system to open the door across the corridor from your bedroom without using a key but this makes a very loud buzzing noise each time. None of this is too bad unless your neighbours are a family with children who are crossing the corridor every two or three minutes from 7am! Or the previous night a drunken couple who keep carrying things between the two rooms at 2am! Clearly the hotel can't be held responsible for the inconsiderate behaviour of its guests but the design is flawed and you risk a very bad night of sleep or a row with your neighbours. It's a shame as everything else is so right but I really can't recommend the Casa Camper.

<Content>Be careful of the rip off We are seasoned travlers who have been around the world several times. We booked four rooms for a family of 11 traveling to Barcelona and staying for one night prior to boarding a cruise ship. We had spent several hours with AMX travel including calling the hotel in order to make sure that there were no problems. We had booked four suites. Our AMX travel counselor had called ahead and found out that each suite would accomodate up to three persons and we were quoted a price of 235.00 euro's per room for up to three people per room. Since there were 11 of us this would be great ( there were seven adults and four children 14 and under). Anyway, once we got there everything was fine and we checked in early as requested. We spent over two hours trying to reason with these people, to no avail. The rooms were small but nice. However,being ripped off for an additional 180. Euro's was not pleasant. So... be careful with this hotel.

<Author>EstherD
<Content>huge telephone bill We stayed 5 days at the casa camper. the service was nice and very helpful. However there were two flaws. One of them is that at the day we checked in at the hotel, we asked how much it will cost to make international calls. The girl at the entrance told us about $1 for every 5 minutes which sounds very reasonable, and not a rip -off price as many hotels are taking. However when we received the bill at the end of our stay, we had to pay $23 for 13 minutes of call time. There were a few calls that no one even answered (e.g. a 3 second call for $0.40 and no answering machine answered).The other issue is that our friends stayed in Barcelona and they came to visit us, and the hotel personnel let them in, while at the end the bill showed $14.10 for this visit. Nobody told us that there is a fee involved for letting our friends in. We should have known this fact before letting people in.Besides these flaws the stay was ok, but the hotel is very simple and the price (235 euro) is definitely not worth the stay. We stayed one night at the marina hotel which cost a little more (280 euros) but was definitely a 5 star hotel. If the free food is important for you, think about all the delicious food that you can taste at the streets of Barcelona. This hotel is nice, but the price is too high for what you get, and for me it is very important to get the real facts before you pay (telephone and friends visit).

<Author>J&ALondon
<Content>A refreshing concept Casa Camper exceeded our expectations, even though we'd read all the good reviews of it on this site. It embodies an entire concept within one hotel.The stylish interior design and sustainability ethic can be seen from its website and is every bit as good as it looks there, attention to detail especially. What you can't see in advance is the atmosphere and exceptional attitude of the staff who take trouble to make you feel genuinely welcome (not the I've-been-trained to-say-this-fake-smile-have-a-nice-day you find pretty much everywhere else). The free all day snack idea and ability to take your breakfast up on to the roof terrace added even more to the sense that you are allowed to relax and feel at home. This works even if, as we did, you stay for just a weekend. The place fits you, not the reverse.If we go back to Barcelona, and we hope we will, we would not consider staying anywhere else.

<Author>Bowen_Family
<Content>A magical experience We very recently had a weekend break at Casa Camper with some good friends to celebrate a birthday. It was the best hotel experience any of us have ever had. I had asked for a bottle of Cava to be waiting in our friends room and not only had they remembered to do this (chilling in an ice bucket, ofcourse) but they had also made a small birthday cake with candle and left a lovely note for her. The hotel is ultra modern and very stylish - but somehow manages to have a real warmth about it. The 24/7 food was fantastic (the cooked breakfast was superb) and because all the food is included in the price, it really made it very good value. It is exceptionally child friendly yet child-free couples would love it also. I can't imagine staying anywhere else if we visit Barcelona again. At one point, sitting on their roof terrace with a view of the rooftops of the city, sipping chilled wine and tasting their delicious snacks we tried to invent a new holiday game - If you could improve one thing about this hotel... what would it be? and we were all lost for ideas. It is as if the owners have brain stormed everything people look for in a hotel and then gone on to make it happen. The only suggestion I can think of is... we need one in every city!
