<Author>funnymom
<Content>Happy Campers Our family of 5, including a teenager, an eleven year-old and a six-year old, stayed here in early August. We LOVED this hotel, and our children rated their stay in this hotel the high-point of our entire two-week trip to Northern Spain. Our boys shared a room with twin beds, my husband and I had a room with a queen-sized bed, and the lounge across the hall allowed our six-year old to have a room of her own. The snacks downstairs were delicious and much appreciated. The modern decor was edgy, without being jarring, and was in keeping with the high-style elsewhere in the City. But, best of all were the warm and helpful staff. Due to the trouble in Heathrow, our return flight was cancelled. The staff, on no notice, found rooms for us, so that we had a place to stay until we could be re-booked back to the States. I would absolutely stay here again.

<Author>restlesstraveler
<Content>Super-hip oasis... If you go, spring for the suite -- pricy, but worth every bit of the money. The hip design and attention to detail are fabulous -- from the hammock in the living room to the sliding doors separating the spaces. The hotel has every amenity you'd want for an urban vacation (great shower, free broadband internet access via a terminal, flat panel TV, etc) plus some that are unique and cool (eco-friendly water re-use in the bathrooms, free sodas, juices and snacks -- including bottled cokes, etc). There's no gym or pool, but you'll get your exercise from walking around the city. Be sure to grab a bottle of wine and hang out for a bit on the penthouse floor ... great view and great spot to soak in all the buzz from below in the city. There are cool outdoor cafes as well nearby (on the same or adjacent side streets, slightly away from the madness of La Rambla) for afternoon or late night dining.

<Author>kjvColorado
<Content>Loved the hotel- go for a suite we spent 4 great nights here last month and loved the place. great service, wonderful location (a funky but ultra safe neighborhood, so if your tastes run 5th avenue stay elsewhere) and loved the free snacks and drinks all day (they should consider padding the seats fo the metal benches in the central lounge and breakfast area). one piece of advice- the suites have the lounge and bedroom connected (as opposed to being across the hall in the regular rooms) and we thought that made the lounge much more useable and made the room much more spacious.by the way- the person who said the rooms were Ikea is wrong. The location is also nearly ideal - close enough to the bustle of La Ramblas, Placa Catalunya and the metro, yet just tucked away in a quaint and quiet block.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Casa Camper - fantastic!! My partner and I have just returned from our holiday in Barcelona where we stayed at Casa Camper. We picked the hotel largely based on other reviews read on Trip Advisor and, I have to say, all positive reviews are 100% correct. It is a lovely, lovely hotel and the staff are fantastic. We've stayed at similar 'pitched' hotels (The Clift in San Francisco, The Hudson in New York, Beau Rivage in Nice) and we both thought Casa Camper was the best of the lot! Where to start? The staff are so welcoming and friendly - nothing is too much trouble and they make you feel at home straight away. The rooms - we paid a little extra and stayed in a suite and it was worth every penny. With standard rooms I don't know about crossing the corridor to the lounge - I think we'd remain cocooned just in the bedroom and the suite has the luxury of both areas 'as one' - but, who knows?! The showers were fab, the beds were the most comfortable I've slept in and the rooms pleasantly quiet. The hammock was great to chill in after a strenous day at the shops or on the beach!The 24 hour snacks are a great idea and really healthy - perfect for a quick snack to stave off hunger pangs before the late night Spanish dining! Breakfasts, too, were delicious and the chef is happy to prepare any egg based dish for you. If not, there are croissants, fresh fruit, ensimadas, yogurts, bread, coffee, juices etc etc.The district is great too - very arty and cool. There are nice restaurants nearby (turn left out of the hotel and first left again) but don't expect to tuck into anything until post 9pm. For cocktails head to Rita Blue on Placa St Augusti (sp?) - 5 minutes walk away. So, all in all a brilliant hotel and one we'll definitely be returning too - hopefully time and time again.

<Author>LouiseandKeith
<Content>High Expectations... I wanted somewhere a bit special for my partners surprise birthday trip to Barcelona but have to say after relying on previous reviews of this hotel my high expectations were left a little short of the mark.The location is great as other reviewers have mentioned,ideal for metros/aerobuses/taxis and tourist bus tours and despite being very near La Rambla, not noisy at night.Service also was also very good-all the staff were very helpful and happy to make many recommendations as to where to go/eat etc in Barcelona. Sitges beach was a lovely tip,a beautiful old town with wonderful shops,quaint winding streets and fab fish restaurants on the seafront-a 35 minute train ride from Barcelona.However 2 nights reception booked restaurants for us,both of which were rather snooty and pretentious (one in Sarria and one at the top of a large tower in Port Olympia). Service was poor and prices high. Probably better to stick to the smaller local restaurants tucked down the many side streets or on the sea front/harbour.Where the hotel fell down in our opinion,was the rooms. They are very 'IKEA' in style and not very cosy to come back to. As the whole room is painted red,they felt very dingy and the only fresh air in the bedrooms was from a tiny window round the corner from the bedroom in the toilet. This wasnt helped by the fact our room smelt very damp/mildewy (Room 32) though this could have just been a leak. Although there was a nice big shower ,after 3 days of walking for miles each day (pretty unavoidable if you want to see as much as you can of the city),it would have been fantastic to come back and be able to soothe you aches and pains away in a bath. The 'lounge' room across from the hall feels like a bit of an afterthought and isnt really a comfortable or practical place to relax although you can get some fresh air in here by opening the balcony doors.For a hotel in this price range (265 EUROS per night) we would expect facilities such as Sky (not just good old BBC World!),cd player,dvd player (there's a space in the wall for them but they are having problems with them at the moment) and a bath.Overall, location and service good but room disappointing,I think they are trying too hard to be hip and have lost some of the home comforts along the way-would love a return visit to Barcelona but would stay somewhere else next time.

Fantastic bathroom, super comfy large bed, safe, digital radio, and a lounge area with flatscreen tv, sofa, lamps, balcony and hammock.The free food and drink was fresh and the menu changed regularly. We took a tray of food and drink up to the lovely sun terrace each afternoon to relax after sightseeing before a relaxed night out.The Hotel is being cleaned almost 24 hrs a day and as you can imagine was absolutely spotless at all times. Our room was serviced each morning and prepared again each evening.The staff could not help us enough and I mean from the front of house to domestics. Every taste was catered for. The french guy that served us each morning was one of the nicest, friendly helpful staff I have ever encoutered at a hotel breakfast session! The cost is by no means cheap but after knocking off the money that one saves from beautiful breakfasts and free food and drink this makes it a rather good rate for what you get in return in my opinion.Take our advice and stop in a suite in this hotel. Do not stop anywhere else. Take the aerobus 3.50euros from the airport to Rambla and you are then just an easy five minute walk from the best hotel in Barcelona. Actually this is the best Hotel we have ever stayed in and we have stayed in a few. From Sydney to New York to London you will not get better service than you will get at Casa Camper Barcelona!

<Content>Home Away From Home How often do you go to a hotel and return home with ideas for how to make your own home as cozy as the hotel? Always looking for a place to hang things in a hotel room or at home? Camper has a shaker style peg rack across an entire wall. Wish you had a chocolate on your pillow but trying to drop 10 extra pounds? Camper the Walking Society eases the sense of deprivation by putting a button on your pillow that says walking is for lovers that reminds you that chocolate isn't everything. Because of Casa Camper, our home away from home, my fiance and I had the impression that we weren't visiting Barcelona for a week, but truly living there. If you want to experience the essence of genuine hospitality in the heart of Barcelona, this is the place for you!

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>This Casa is for you! My husband and I just spent four days at the Casa Camper. Despite the jet lag, I wanted to write this while it's fresh in my mind. We absolutely loved the Casa Camper. The location was ideal - just a few blocks from Placa Catalunya - the primary hub for bus and train travel. However, do not take the train from the airport. The line is under construction, making the train changes with bags a real headache. Get on one of the blue Aerobuses, which is very inexpensive and drops you in the exact same place as the train. It's an easy walk to the hotel from there. The great thing about the Casa Camper was that it is two short blocks off La Rambla, so it was quiet yet close to everything. The room was a delight. Comfy king sized bed; great linens; super strong showerhead. My husband loved the electronic adjustable window shading device which controlled light and views to the vertical garden outside. (Too hard to describe - you just have to see it!) The breakfast/free self-serve snack area was a dream. After a long day of seeing the sites, you can grab a cold juice and head to the rooftop terrace. (They also sell beer and wine in the lobby, which makes for a great treat on the terrace as well.) Staff was extremely helpful and good with english. The public corridor splits your bedroom and living room (lounge), but we didn't spend any time in the lounge anyway. If you're up for a well designed, clean, new hotel, you can't go wrong at the Casa Camper.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>There is only one place to stay in Barcelona This is the third trip i have used tripadvisor to help pick my hotel. Each trip has been a roaring success. My advice would be that if you cannot get a room in Casa Camper, rebook your flights to a day you can get a room. Casa camper is run by the friendliest (and some of the prettiest) people in Spain. This is in stark contrast to the museum staffwho are generally curt and unhelpful (but not necessarily ugly). The hotel is spotlessly clean. You use your keycard to access the lobby. This safeguards a multitude of free snacks available 24hours a day. The central location allows you to drop shopping bags off, and recharge on salads, juice and redbull in the process. Alteratively take a trayful of food upto the 6th floor to relax on the terrace, or take it across the corridor from you room, where everyone has their own individual mini lounge for reading about Barcelona in the provided colour guidebook, lying in the hammock or lazing on the foldout sofa (which could accommodate a third sleeping person).Try the camper owned Foodballs cafe two doors down once you've emptied the kitchen of its delights. Your room has the perfect shower experience. There are trendy hotel slippers, flat screen TVs, a radio, safe and bizarrely a step ladder in the room. Only complaints are that the beds were twin, but were easily pushed together. It took me 2 days to work out the light switches and how to unplug the basin (little knob behind the tap!). I also read somewhere that the rooms have a CD player, so i brought some discs. This was the not the case, but i didn't have time to listen to them anyway. Holidaysnaps and hotel pics are available on my website via www.shoddyweasel.com

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Couldn't rate it more highly We decided to treat ourselves as we usually go low budget and we are so glad we did. The hotel is wonderful and everything said about the staff is true. The little details and the quirky design is what firstly appealed to us, but, the friendly staff, wonderful food and relaxed atmosphere were the icing on the cake. The location is fantastic, don't even consider getting a cab from the airport, hop on the bus and for 鈧?.75 it takes you directly to Place de Catalunya. From there, stroll down La Rambla and it is literally the 2nd right which is a little alleyway called Pla莽a dels 脌'ngels that is very safe. Keep going and you will end up on Carrer Elisabets which is where the hotel is. It takes about 5 minutes to walk from Place de Catalunya.Back to the hotel! The showers are heaven (a small but often overlooked part of hotels). We loved looking out to the garden of plants in the morning and it is completely private. We rarely used the room across the hall but it is nice. The only down side was that our beds were 2 single beds which we didn't realise and I'm not sure was there an option of a double. The terrace is lovely to relax on in the evenings with the sun shining down on you and you can bring snacks from the bar up which is great. The food was fantastic and all free and the soup was home made. The breakfast was delicious too. All in all we loved casa camper and we will return there without hesitation.

<Author>AAA Trip Advisor Member
<Content>As good as the reviews Just got back from a 4 day stay at the Casa Camper. We booked the hotel on the strength of the reviews on this site and were not disappointed. It has a superb location in a quiet street just off La Rambla. The staff are excellent. Nothing is too much trouble and if you are happy to do your own thing they are happy to let you. A major pluspoint for us is that it is a non-smoking hotel. In a country where it seems it is compulsary that you smoke this is truly superb.The rooms are different. We had a suite which comprised a living room, a bedroom and a bathroom and we found it very modern and very luxurious. A particularly nice touch is the free snacks. 24*7 you can get free tea, coffee, soup, soft drinks, fruit and snacks. This is particularly nice if you pop back to the hotel at points during the day.There is a terrace on the roof which is nice to just sit and chill. The view isn't the best but that's hardly the fault of the hotel. One particular nice touch was on checking out in the morning we asked about leaving our luggage as we had a late flight. This, as in most hotels, was no problem, however, they told us that on our return we could still help ourselves to the free snacks. This kind of customer service goes a long way to explaining why they are so highly rated. We would highly recommend the hotel.

<Author>FSA
<Content>I'm in love I can't add any more than the other reviewers. This is the best experience of staying in a hotel that I have ever had, and I've stayed in a fair old few, including a 5* in Barcelona on a previous trip. Everything is so well thought out, and all the details made our stay just perfect, the only problem was enjoying the hotel and the room as much as we did that we were in danger of never leaving the front door and exploring all that Barcelona has to offer! The 24 hour free cafe is fantastic, I wasn't expecting such variety and quailty of food - to the extent that we didn't explore the local tapas bars as much as we expected as we always seemed to be within easy reach of the hotel!If you want a bog standard corporate soulless hotel with the usual trappings such as a mini bar in the room and gym or swimmimg pool, then this probably won't be for you. If you want a 'quirky' ambiance, perfect location, excellent personal service with friendly, helpful staff, rooms that provide everything you could ever want including the most comfortable bed ever, then you will not do better than Casa Camper.

<Author>TomSleaford
<Content>Friendly, Relaxed, Foodie, but a little overpriced? I can confirm virtually all of the previous reviewers comments. We arrived tired after a difficult trip from the airport, trains are not operating normally from El Prat at the moment, and were welcomed with a friendly intro and the opportunity to grab free drinks. The rooms are as good as described, though if you are someone who likes fabrics and freebies, you will be disappointed. The roof terrace is very pleasant and gives a good view over some of the city. However, if you are seeking an escape from the piped music, it is louder here than in the lobby.Some reviewers have underplayed the snacks, in my opinion. If you like organic juices, salads, sandwiches and home made soup, this is your kind of place. The only drawback to this is that they are so good we were tempted to eat in on a couple of nights and did not sample what the city had to offer. My tip would be the organic mandarin juice and the Vichy Catalan - possibly an acquired taste.Staff are young, pleasant and mulit-lingual. My wife tells me the young men must have been selected for looks as well as ability but I don't feel fully qualified to judge. At any rate all staff will take time to discuss your stay and give you excellent advice.I only have 2 quibbles. Firstly we couldn't get our air conditioning to work on the first night and neither could the hotel staff. (You can open a window but those skaters don't let up until the early hours of the morning.) Secondly, it was slightly expensive for a three star hotel - though we had a suite so you could stay more cheaply. That said , if you were staying with childern it would work out very well.My final point would be to agree with others that this is a little like staying in a friend's flat whilst they are away, in all the best ways. If you seeking a relaxing, friendly, centrally located hotel and don't mind paying a little more for it, than this is an ideal hotel.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Two for two with Trip Advisor My wife, daughter (16) and I stayed at Casa Camper from 06-10 April 2006 primarily due to the reviews posted on Trip Advisor. We couldn't have been more pleased. Some specifics:1. Service - We had an overnight flight from JFK to BCN and reserved the room for a day rate so we could sleep when we arrived. We had three people and the lounge was not made up as a bed. The staff did that immediately (within five minutes). That response is typical of the service you will receive. Gemma, at the front desk, was particularly helpful in getting us dinner rreservations and giving us maps. Quick point: mention La Rambla to the taxi driver at the airport if they don't know the location, as ours didn't.2. The Room - is very quiet, despite the location so close to La Rambla. It is also extremely functional. The wall has 27 hooks (I counted them) for hanging various objects. By the sink is a double-paned window that opens into a courtyard with six floors of large plants, which make it very pleasant when you use the sink. At night, a green industrial louver comes down and that makes the room very dark and excellent to sleep in. The shower is overhead, large and has plenty of hot water. I used the lounge to sleep in while the ladies had the bed. It worked out just fine. You can try the hammock in the lounge if you wish. Final point - check out the roof. The view is wonderful.3. Food - Breakfast was much better than most other hotels where we have stayed. Eggs are cooked to order. Fresh fruits are sliced thin. There are a variety of croissants and breads. The food area is used as a snack bar from 1100 on. This is a great idea. We used it for a late snack once and it worked out well.4.Location - For walking tours off La Rambla, it is terrific. It is also close to the tourist buses, which I would recommend. Finally, there are a good number of restaurants within walking distance. We ate at La Cariocoles and La Fonda, both on Carrer dels Escudellers. The latter prix fixe is a good bargain. Line up at 2015 for a table. El Pinafor was more formal. Get a reservation here. Sagardi, Carrer Argenteria near the Cathedral, has excellent tapas. 5.Trip Advisor - We found this hotel through Trip Advisor. It was an excellent choice. We found the previous reviews to be very helpful, and hope this one is helpful also. We are two for two with Trip Advisor (Paris - Hotel Saint Louis Bastille) and will continue to use this service.

We had a suite which was great as you do not have to go across the hall for your living room, it felt like living in your coolest friend's apartment and indeed it was hard to leave the hotel at times. We got a slightly reduced corporate rate through one of the major travel websites. Barcelona is an incredible city and this hotel is in the middle of it all, it is an easy walk from the airport bus so you do not need to take a taxi to or from the airport. We started our 2 week Spain trip here, and the only downside was that this hotel spoiled us for the rest of the trip since no other hotel could measure up. Can't wait to return to Barcelona and would not think of staying anywhere else!

<Content>Fantastic. Really. My husbands' folks live close to Barcelona, so we don't often stay in Barcelona proper, but with family coming over, we decided to go and live the city life for a few days. I've only ever stayed before at Hotel Colon in maybe 95 or 96 (old, old, but atmsospheric sundays on the balcony watching the dancing below).Plus this time we had a 20 month old toddler in tow. And wow. Casa Camper is just fantastic. We've stayed in hundreds of hotels (business travelling everywhere) but this place is unique. First the decor. Then the wonderful service. These guys can't bend further over backwards to make you feel more at home. You'll see the same people at reception checking over your rooms or restocking the cafeteria....there doesn't seem to be a rigid hierarchy so everyone feels responsible and boy, does that work !The rooms were just great. Loved the hammocks and the vertical garden. My one and only criticism of the hotel is that there wasn't quite enough light in the rooms at night. Maybe a few more funky spots ?Fantastic location. The cafeteria versus minibar is a brilliant concept (and if you've ever travelled with young kids, then all those yoghurts, juices, milks, snacks, fruit are a godsend when provided in the room rate of your hotel). Really couldn't find a fault on anything. We had a slight complication (our side!) on billing but they were clear and as helpful as could be and even sent docs by express to clarify (when we were already clear), without us even asking. Exceedingly honest. The eco benefits are all a boost, although if we didn't say it, you wouldn't know it. Can highly recommend renting a bike for a day to see more of the wonderful city. Couldn't recommend this hotel more. And it's been a long time since we've felt that way about a hotel. Just go and ENJOY !

<Author>georgemocha
<Content>Service unlike any other hotel I've stayed in I can only echo the other glowing reviews of the Casa Camper in this website. I stayed there for an all-to-brief visit, with a friend and our two 12-year-olds. Each family had a suite. Everything was terrific from the moment we arrived. The reception staff are genuinely sweet, personable, and most helpful. When we needed to call New York urgently, they just directed us to their phone at the reception desk. The food service is such a great idea that I'm surprised other hotels don't copy it. The food area is open 24/7 and is well stocked with all sorts of snacks, drinks, sandwiches, salads, and homemade soup, made fresh daily. Breakfast was great with the kitchen providing eggs if desired. By the second day, when we came down for breakfast our table for 4 was already set for us, with little personal touches remembered from our preferences of the day before. There are no additional charges for the food. The girls thought it was terrific that they could go down in their pajamas for chips etc. at midnight. The room was also terrific including the hammocks, excellent linens, reading lights above the bed, the bathroom, and the overall cleanliness (no grotty carpeting). I loved the system of hooks along the wall (very Shaker) to hang coats, pocketbooks, shopping bags - very effective to reduce the usual hotel room clutter.I can't rate this hotel highly enough.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Perfect Location  We just got back from a 5 day stay at Casa Camper. Only a five minute walk off the bustling La Rambla, Casa Camper was a wonderful city getaway on a quiet side street. The staff was kind and helpful. The bedroom is roomy and the bathroom overlooks a garden courtyard. The room is VERY quiet and shutters keep the morning light out. The rain shower was perfect after a day of wandering the wonderful streets of Barcelona. The living room across the hall had a small balcony overlooking the street (more like an alley as there is not regular traffic) which was a picturesque vision of a Barcelona neighborhood. An elementary school is across the way and the University is nearby-- good people watching from the balcony at any time of day. Breakfast is a treat -- wonderful cafe amb llet and selection of meats, pastries, breads, yogurt, juices, and eggs. The 24 hour snack bar was great for a midday bite, or for a late night drink. If you want to go out for a quick bite, there were several cafes and tapas bars half a block down the street that did not feel too touristy. A computer in the lobby with free internet and printer was a helpful resource too.Overall, Casa Camper and the staff felt like it fit right into the neighborhood--young and hip without any pretense, and with a good sense of humor thrown in.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Perfect location, fun stay The hotel is in a perfect location - a minute's walk from La Ramblas (the main street) and Placa De Catalunya (the main square) but tucked away in a side street away from noise. The hotel staff are very friendly; on our first day the daytime receptionist gave us a map which was invaluable to us during our stay and recommended places to eat and suggested areas to visit which was really helpful.We decided to opt for a suite rather than the standard room. The standard rooms have a bedroom and bathroom on one side of the corridor and another room comprising lounge with sofa bed, hammock, table and on the other side of the corridor. A weird concept. We didn't fancy the idea of crossing the corridor to get to our lounge, and probably wouldn't have used it so booked a suite which was all-in-one. The suite comprised a bathroom at one end with a rainfall shower (bliss) and a handheld shower attachment both inside the bath. Fixtures are modern (chrome by Brabantia) and decor relaxing; walls are blood-red, floors are charcoal slate and furnishings are stark white or red.From the bathroom you enter the bedroom, with a king-sized bed in the suite. There are sliding wooden doors between the bathroom and lounge which when closed you feel 'cocooned' in the windowless bedroom - all sense of time evaporates; there is no clock in the bedroom so it would be wise to take an alarm clock! There is a safe and digital radio in the bedroom - I'm not sure if this is unique to the suite or provided in standard rooms too.The lounge consists of a hammock (which I loved having an afternoon doze in!), flat-screen TV on which you can receive BBC World and CNN, double-sofa bed and table and chairs. There is air-conditioning and heating, however it seems to default to a particular temperature after a period of time, although is quick to warm up again. The lobby area houses a canteen area - the hotel says it doesn't believe in mini-bars so provides a self-service area where sandwiches, pastries, drinks, fruit, salads are provided free of charge to guests, which on first thought seems hugely generous...however on reflection the hotel is probably saving a fortune by not having to fund a hotel restaurant and staff. However it's a pleasant and quirky addition to the hotel...the food is basic and isn't anything to write home about, but serves well as fuel. There is a 'restaurant' next door owned by Camper called FoodBall. This is just odd. The seating is reminiscent of stadium bleachers and your chair is a wicker mat, and your food compressed into a ball. Hence the name. The 'restaurant' is a room covered with posters and graffiti. So unless you're anything but an ageing hippy or staunch eco-warrior type, I would suggest this is not the type of place you would want to spend your Saturday night in! However, we didn't try it and the 'ball' could well rise above it's surroundings. For women with long hair, I would suggest bringing your own hairdryer...there is one in the bathroom although it is so weak it would take hours to dry anything....although I must say this is not unique to Casa Camper and is the case in most hotels I've stayed in. The light in the bathroom is stark and unforgiving and with mirrors on both wals you get a 360 degree view of yourself which can be a shock!We decided the take the Metro to Sagradda Famille and it was really easy to use - the ticket machines display Engish instructions and a single journey cost 1.15 Euros. We found a few great restaurants while we were there and can recommend the following: For a basic, low-cost Spanish meal - try the restaurant on the right hand side of the road if you are walking from the hotel to La Ramblas - it has ham hanging in the window. I am veggie but the carnivores told me the meat was fab...for 4 of us the entire bill came to 39 Euros which included wine. El Pintor - tucked away off Place St. Jaume in the Barri Gotic (Gothic Quarter) - perfect for a romantic meal...expect a good meal, but not a cheap one. The best we ate at. My carnivore boyfriend was in heaven with the cured ham.Cerveceria Catalana - Tapas place on Calle de Mallorca - the hotel receptionist recommended this to us...it is always hugely busy...a real mad house but frequented by locals and the Tapas is fantastic. Overall, we would highly recommend Casa Camper to anyone wanting to experience a quirky and fun stay and if we were to go back to Barcelona would not hesitate in staying there again. It is not in the same league as the luxury hotels of Barcelona - do not expect sweeping staircases and chandeliers - it is a different concept to those hotels. The hotel's main benefit is probably its location - it is perfect.

<Author>travelinhope
<Content>close to perfection My wife and I stayed at Casa Camper for four nights in mid-October, on the basis of the rave reviews. It's everything that's been written about it. Absolutely perfect location; rooms spotlessly clean, bathroom in a different league from other hotels and beds totally comfortable. Staff beautiful and very helpful -they extended our check out time until late afternoon because we had a late night flight.However...not sure the separate sitting rooms work very well, particularly on the lower floors. They are rather gloomy because of the neighbouring building across the narrow, interesting (and almost traffic-free) street. Didn't feel comfortable in ours -despite the hammock! Higher up or a suite would probably be a better bet. Also with the dark red and black colour schemes it can feel a little claustrophobic. Maybe it was just the unusual weather - it rained for a lot of the time but you tended to lose touch with the outside world. The remedy would be to take regular trips to the 6th floor outdoor terrace which gave a tremendous view.But all in all as close to the perfect combination of style and service as is likely to be found. Just book a room above the second floor.......

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>#1! i just got back from a 10-day trip to barcelona and stayed for 9 nights at casa camper. stayed in both a room with the mini-lounge and in a suite (got an upgrade a couple of days later at no extra charge). the chic minimalist decor succeeds (what the Standard in LA must have aimed to be but dismally failed). everything was immaculate--from the sheets to the in-house cafeteria. i totally love the row of hooks that lined the wall. and the rooms were large by european standards (even larger than most boutique hotel suites i've stayed in in the US). but enough about the rooms. what really sets the hotel apart is the staff and the service they provide. in most hotels, a cold, crisp manner is mistaken for professionalism and efficiency. at casa camper, professionalism is coupled with a genuinely friendly attitude and warmth. i had the unfortunate luck of having my wallet stolen during this trip, and upon learning this, the staff immediately assisted me in contacting the local credit card offices. i didn't even have to ask!the location is great. i love that it is within walking distance from all the different districts. its closeness to barrio chino gives it an unpretentious appeal.i would definitely stay here during my next visit to barcelona.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>What a cool hotel!! We just returned from an amazing stay at the Casa Camper. I have to admit I researched and double researched every hotel in the Barcelona area and time and time again this hotel just seemed to stand out from the rest. Everything about this hotel makes your trip even more enjoyable (Especially the shower!!).There's not much more I can add to the other reviews because they all tell the many extras this hotel has to offer. We opted for a suite and I would definitely recommend it. It is so convenient to have a lounge area connected right to the bedroom but still separated by a sliding wood door, if needed. It does not get more convenient than to be able to grab a snack or beverage on your way out to tour the city. The location of this hotel is great, just steps from Las Ramblas and a short walking distance to many of the city's other attractions (Gothic Quarter, Port area etc.) We were lucky enough to stay there during Le Mercer (a holy day(s) full of many festivities) and easily walked to many of the concerts, parades and activities happening all over the city.If you are looking for a chic but comfortable hotel with an extremely helpful staff and all the extras for a decent price, Casa Camper is the way to go!!

<Content>Welcome to Coolsville, population... us :) We stayed at the Camper for a few nights before our cruise. There's not much I can add to the latest review aside from saying that they're dead on.Decor is fantastic, immediately had visions of renovating my bathroom at home after seeing the shower. The one thing I can say about both Barcelona hotels we stayed at is Fantastic water pressure!!! The absolute most satisfying thing about this hotel was the pricing structure. Yes, it is pricey, but the snack area, morning breakfasts and internet access is all included so you pay once and that's it.Only thing to add is FYI, the hotel is a very short walk from P. Cataluyna, so feel confident to take the airport bus to Cataluyna and walk to the hotel. (provided you have rollers on your suit case... like a 5min walk)

<Author>sparklerhino
<Content>Fantastically cool hotel Found this hotel through TripAdvisor: read the other reviews  beleive them. Stayed for 4 nights at the beginning of September at this cool trendy hotel  loved it. The design  styling of the hotel is fatastic, very urban  beautifully done. The tentenpie is a nice touch,  means you can just snack when you want to. The beds are large  comfortable,  the showers are fantastic. I'd be tempted to go for a suite next time, just to avoid crossing the corridor to the lounge, although, the corridor is not exacly a problem!The staff are soooo good. They were all, without exception, beautiful to behold, trendy, and genuinely helpful, friendly  accommodating - none of that detached disinterest I have experienced in hotels all over the world!The hotel is in an interesting area, may be slightly too 'developing' for some people, as it's very much a still-up--coming area, but this wasn't a problem. There are some great restaurants in the vicinity too (although avoid 'Neen' (or Carmelitas, which was the alternative name) as my husband got food poisining there  spent the entire next day wiped out as a result.).This is a great hotel if you like urban cool. It you like glitz, then maybe not for you, but I would definintely use it again.
